Defining Nazar: The Path to Knowledge
The commentator defines nazar and distinguishes its two meanings, with a note on its linguistic range.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two technical definitions of nazar in kalam and how it functions to produce knowledge.

Core Idea
Nazar is the structured use of known premises to uncover unknown truths.

This lesson unpacks the foundational term nazar (speculative reasoning), which is the engine of all theological argument in kalam. The text defines it first as the arrangement of known premises to attain an unknown conclusion, then as thought that leads to knowledge or belief. Understanding these definitions is essential before engaging with any kalam proofs.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic passage and its translation slowly. Notice the two definitions presented: one as 'tartib' (arrangement) and one as 'fikr' (thought).
Pay attention to the example of the syllogism about the world's change.
2
Identify the key distinction
Reflect on why nazar is defined in two ways. The first emphasizes logical arrangement, the second emphasizes the mental process. Consider how each captures a different aspect of reasoning.
The linguistic note about 'nazar' being homonymous between sight and thought may help.
3
Consider the schools' differences
The footnote discusses how correct nazar leads to knowledge: by rational necessity (al-Juwayni), by custom (al-Ash'ari), or by generation (Mu'tazila). Think about the implications for theological methodology.
This debate shows that even definitions carry theological weight.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حقيقة النظر الموصل إلى المعرفة
ترتيب أمور معلومة (١) لِيُتَوصَّل بها - أي بترتيبها - إلى مجهول، أي: إلى علمه ، كترتيب الصُّغرى مع الكُبرى في قولنا: (العالم متغيّر (٢) وكلُّ متغيّر حادث) فإِنَّه مُوصل للعلم بحدوث العالم ، المجهول(۳) قبل ذلك الترتيب
وعرَّفه شيخ الاسلام بأنَّه : فِكْر يؤدي(٤) إلى علم أو اعتقادِ النفس في المحسوسات فيسمى تخيلاً. وعطف الفكر على الإبصار مغاير ، والنظر إن تعدى بـ (إلى) كان بمعنى الإبصار ، وإن تعدى بـ (في) كان بمعنى الفكر. وعلى ذلك: فالنظر مشترك بين الإبصار والفكر .
(١) قوله: (معلومة) أي حاضرة عند العقل تصوريا كان أو تصديقيا، يقينيا أو ظنيا أو جهلا، واشترط في الأمور المرتبة العلم.. لاستحالة التوصل بما ليس بحاصل بعد. قوله: (إلى مجهول) إنما اشترط في الأمر المطلوب الجهل .. لاستحالة تحصيل الحاصل. الشنواني.
(۲) اعلم أنَّ العالم مكوّن من أعراض أي أمور تقوم بغيرها كالحركة، والسكون، والطول، :
والقصر، والبياض، والسواد، ونحو ذلك . و جواهر: أي أمور تقوم بأنفسها كذات زيد ، والجدار ، ونحوهما. وأنَّ المُتغير على الحقيقة الأعراض، وتغيرها ثابت بالمشاهدة . وأما الجواهر فإنَّها لا تتغيّر في أنفسها، وإِنَّما تتغيّر الأعراض الملازمة لها، فيكون تغيرها بتغير الأعراض الملازمة لها. محي.

(۳) قوله: (المجهول) صفة لحدوث
منه
(٤) قوله: (فكر يؤدي هذا التعريف أعمُّ مما قبله ، وهو للأصوليين، أعني أصول الدين وأصول الفقه . وأخذُ الفكر جنسا للنظر مبني على مساواته له وهو المشهور ، خلافا لمن زعم أنه أعم فمنع تفسيره به، وخرج بقوله: (فكر يؤدي) فكر لا يؤدي كأن تفكر تفكرا لم يصل به إلى المطلوب كأكثر حديث النفس ؛ فلا يسمى نظرا الشنواني. وكون النظر الصحيح مؤديا إلى العلم إما أن يكون بطريق اللزوم العقلي كالتلازم بين الجوهر والعرض ، فوجود أحدهما بدون الآخر مستحيل عقلي لا تتعلق به القدرة ، بل إما أن يوجدا معا أو يُعدما ، وهذا مذهب إمام الحرمين الجويني، وهو ما رجحه الأمير والشنواني في حاشيتيهما . وإما أن يكون التلازم عاديا يقبل التخلف ، وهو مذهب الشيخ الأشعري. وقالت المعتزلة بالتَّولد وهو: أن يوجِبَ الفعل لفاعله شيئا آخر. وقالت الفلاسفة: بالإيجاب
والتعليل .
Clarification of the reality of nazar (speculative reasoning) that leads to knowledge: the arrangement of known things (1) to arrive by means of them—i.e., by arranging them—at an unknown thing, i.e., at knowledge of it, like the arrangement of the minor premise with the major premise in our statement: 'The world is changing (2) and everything changing is originated,' for it leads to knowledge of the world’s origination, the unknown (3) before that arrangement. And the Shaykh al-Islam defined it as: thought that leads (4) to knowledge or belief of the soul regarding sensible things, in which case it is called imagination. And the conjunction of thought with sight is in a different sense. Nazar, if it is transitive with 'ila' (to), has the meaning of sight; if transitive with 'fi' (in), it has the meaning of thought. Thus nazar is shared between sight and thought. (1) His saying: 'known things' means present in the mind, whether conceptual or assent, certain or probable or ignorant; he stipulated that the arranged things be known because it is impossible to reach something that is not yet obtained. His saying: 'to an unknown' he stipulated that the sought thing be unknown because it is impossible to obtain what is already obtained. al-Shanwani. (2) Know that the world is composed of accidents—i.e., things that subsist in others like motion, rest, length, shortness, whiteness, blackness, and the like—and substances: i.e., things that subsist in themselves like the essence of Zayd, the wall, and the like. And that changing in reality is [a property] of accidents, and their change is established by observation. As for substances, they do not change in themselves, but rather the accidents inseparable from them change, so their change is by the change of the accidents inseparable from them. Muhyi. (3) His saying: 'the unknown' is a description of 'origination'. (4) His saying: 'thought that leads'—this definition is more general than the previous one, and it belongs to the usuliyyun, i.e., specialists in usul al-din and usul al-fiqh. Taking 'thought' as a genus for nazar is based on their equivalence, which is the well-known view, contrary to those who claim it is more general and thus prevented interpreting nazar by it. By his saying 'thought that leads' he excludes thought that does not lead, like one who thinks without reaching the sought object, as in most inner speech; this is not called nazar. al-Shanwani. And that correct nazar leads to knowledge either by way of rational necessity, like the necessary concomitance between substance and accident, so that the existence of one without the other is rationally impossible and not subject to power; rather they either exist together or are both non-existent—this is the madhhab of Imam al-Haramayn al-Juwayni, which al-Amir and al-Shanwani preferred in their glosses. Or the concomitance is customary, admitting of exception—this is the madhhab of Shaykh al-Ash'ari. The Mu'tazila said by 'tawallud' (generation): that the act necessitates for its agent something else. The philosophers said by necessitation and causation.
Source pages p. 169

Commentary
This passage defines the technical term 'nazar' (speculative reasoning) and clarifies its meaning and scope. The commentator begins by stating that the passage is a clarification of the reality of nazar that leads to knowledge. He then gives the first definition: nazar is the arrangement of known things to arrive at an unknown. He illustrates this with the classic kalam syllogism: 'the world is changing, and everything changing is originated.' This syllogism leads to knowledge of the world's origination, which was unknown before the arrangement. The commentator adds a second definition from Shaykh al-Islam (likely al-Ash'ari or a later authority): nazar is thought that leads to knowledge or belief regarding sensible things; if it leads to belief about sensibles, it is called imagination. He then notes a linguistic point: the word 'nazar' is homonymous between sight (when transitive with 'ila') and thought (when transitive with 'fi'). This clarifies that nazar in the technical sense is the latter, but the word shares both meanings. The footnotes expand on the definitions. Footnote 1 explains that 'known things' (معلومة) means present in the mind, whether conceptual or assent, certain or probable, and that the unknown must not be already known. Footnote 2 explains that the world consists of accidents (changing) and substances (not changing in themselves). Footnote 3 is brief. Footnote 4 discusses the second definition: it is more general and applies to usul al-din and usul al-fiqh; it distinguishes nazar from mere thought that does not lead; it also presents a significant kalam discussion on how correct nazar leads to knowledge—either by rational necessity (the view of al-Juwayni) or by customary concomitance (the view of al-Ash'ari), with the Mu'tazila and philosophers having their own views. The commentator does not decisively choose one, but notes preferences.

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think nazar is any random thought or reflection.
Correction: Nazar must be a structured arrangement of known premises that leads to a result; random or aimless thought does not qualify.

Checkpoint
According to the first definition, what is nazar?
A) Sight with the eyes
B) The arrangement of known things to reach an unknown
C) Any thought that occurs to the mind
D) A type of belief

Key Takeaway
Nazar in kalam is not mere thought but the deliberate ordering of knowledge to uncover new truths, forming the core of rational theology.

The Linguistic Definition of Faith (Iman)
The author defines faith linguistically as affirmation and explains its root meaning.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the linguistic definition of faith (iman) as affirmation (tasdiq) and its root meaning of security.

Core Idea
Faith linguistically means heartfelt affirmation, not mere verbal confession.

Before we can discuss the theological dimensions of faith, we must first understand what the word 'iman' means in the Arabic language. The author begins by grounding the discussion in the linguistic definition, which centers on affirmation of truth. He also notes that this definition contrasts with common misunderstandings that reduce faith to speech or actions.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage
Read the passage carefully, noting the key terms 'الإيمان', 'التصديق', and 'الأمن'. See how the author defines faith in relation to security.
2
Understand the linguistic definition
The author states that iman means tasdiq (affirmation), which is acquiescence and acceptance of a judgment as true. The root is 'amn' (security), implying that faith removes fear of rejection.
3
Distinguish linguistic from technical
Notice that after giving the linguistic definition, the author signals that the technical definition is debated. This lesson focuses on the linguistic meaning.

بيان حقيقة الإيمان
الإيمان في اللغة معناه : التصديق ، ومعنى التصديق : الإذعان للحكم وقبوله والاعتراف بكونه صادقا، والأصل فيه: (الأمن) الذي هو ضد الخوف ، وكأنَّ حقيقة قولنا: «آمن فلان» أنه نفى عنه خوف التكذيب والمخالفة .

Explanation of the reality of faith. 18 Explanation of the reality of faith 15. And faith was interpreted as affirmation (al-tasdiq), and speaking in it is the conflict, in reality. And since faith and Islam, by virtue of the application of their concepts (1) — which is what must be believed in — are among the topics of the science of kalam, the author, may Allah have mercy on him, mentioned them, giving precedence to faith due to its originality because it is connected to the heart (2), and the subordination of Islam to it because it is connected to the limbs. He said: (And faith was interpreted) (3) i.e., defined by the majority of the Ash'aris and Maturidis and others. (1) His saying: (the application of their concepts) the concept of faith is inner submission, and the concept of Islam is outer submission, and their application is nothing but what is known necessarily from the religion — including the existence of God, His oneness, and the obligation of prayer and fasting — because it is that for which failure to submit constitutes unbelief, not other things. Thus the application in its entirety is among the topics of this art, even in summary, and as for the remaining rulings, they are among its consequences and completions, without being part of the application on which the concept depends, i.e., what is not necessary, so it does not need to be said: the intended is part of the application, so reflect. (2) His saying: (because it is connected to the heart) i.e., which is the origin of the limbs; because of their subordination to it in soundness and corruption, faith is a condition for the validity of the deeds of the limbs, so reflect. (3) Know first that faith and Islam, by virtue of the application of their concepts — which is what is known necessarily from the religion — are among the topics of the science of kalam, as understood from the author's speech below where he said: (And whoever denies a matter known necessarily). Because of this, the theologians mention them in the topics of kalam, but the authors differ in the place of mentioning them; some authors mention them after completing the topics of divinity, prophethood, and things heard, and some put this topic before all of that, due to the need of one who engages in kalam to know them, and the author followed this path. And know — after that — that the scholars have much speech on explaining the reality of faith, and it is incumbent upon us that we = 175 = explain it to you in a sufficient explanation, saying: Explanation of the reality of faith. Faith in the language means: affirmation (al-tasdiq), and the meaning of affirmation is: acquiescence to the judgment, acceptance of it, and acknowledgment of it being truthful, and its root is (security) which is the opposite of fear, and it is as if the reality of our saying: 'So-and-so believed' is that he removed from himself the fear of denial and opposition. As for faith in the technical sense of the people of the Shari'a, the scholars have differed in defining it according to five opinions:
Source pages p. 176

Commentary
This passage introduces the topic of faith (iman) and begins by giving its linguistic definition. The author first notes that faith and Islam are discussed in kalam because they relate to what must be believed in. He explains why the author of the poem and commentary mentioned faith first: faith is connected to the heart, which is the origin of the limbs, while Islam is connected to the limbs and follows faith. Then he gives the linguistic definition: faith means tasdiq (affirmation), which is acquiescence, acceptance, and acknowledgment of truth. Its root is 'amn (security), opposite of fear; saying 'he believed' means he removed fear of rejection. Finally, he states that the scholars differ on the technical definition, listing five opinions, which will be explained in the next lesson.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you say 'I believe in Allah', do you truly affirm (tasdiq) it in your heart with full acquiescence and acceptance, or is it just a verbal habit? What would change if you really did?
?
The root of iman is 'amn' — security from fear. Do you live with the deep security that comes from knowing the truth? Or do you still worry that your faith might be false? What would it take for you to feel that security?
?
The author says that saying 'So-and-so believed' means he removed from himself the fear of denial and opposition. Are you willing to fully commit to the truth of Islam, even if it means facing ridicule or going against your desires? What holds you back from that complete affirmation?

The Linguistic Meaning of Iman
Linguistic definition of iman with etymology.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the core meaning and etymology of iman in the Arabic language.

Core Idea
Iman linguistically means tasdiq – acceptance and security from fear.

Before diving into theological definitions, Sanusi grounds us in the Arabic word itself. Language gives us the conceptual anchor: iman is not mere belief but active affirmation and a sense of safety. This lesson unpacks that foundation.

Guided Path
1
Read the linguistic definition
Read the Arabic passage for the linguistic definition and its translation. Notice the connection between 'iman' and 'amn' (security).
The definition uses 'tasdiq' which implies acceptance, not just intellectual assent.
2
Understand the root derivation
Sanusi explains that iman comes from 'amn' (the opposite of fear). Consider how the act of believing removes the fear of being contradicted.
3
Reflect on the implication
Ask yourself: why does the author start with language? Because theological terms must be built on clear linguistic foundations.
This prepares you for the technical Shar'i definitions in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حقيقة الإيمان
الإيمان في اللغة معناه : التصديق ، ومعنى التصديق : الإذعان للحكم وقبوله والاعتراف بكونه صادقا، والأصل فيه: (الأمن) الذي هو ضد الخوف ، وكأنَّ حقيقة قولنا: «آمن فلان» أنه نفى عنه خوف التكذيب والمخالفة .
وأما الإيمان في عرف أهل الشرع فقد اختلف العلماء في تحديد معناه على خمسة أقوال: أولها - وهو مذهب جمهور المحققين من الأشاعرة والماتريدية ـ أنَّه : التصديق بما عُلم مجيء النبي به ضرورة تفصيلا فيما عُلم تفصيلا، وإجمالا فيما عُلم إجمالاً ، ومع اتفاقهم على أنَّ حقيقة الإيمان هي ما ذكرنا فحسب اختلفوا في مناط أحكام الآخرة: أهو مجرد هذا التصديق أم هو مع الإقرار باللسان ؟ وقد اشتهر أنَّ الأشعري وأتباعه يقولون: إن هذه هي حقيقة الإيمان، وهذه الحقيقة وحدها هي مناط إجراء أحكام الآخرة، والإقرار إنما يشترط عندهم ليعرف الناس به وجودَ الإيمان عند صاحبه وليُجروا عليه أحكام الدُّنيا ; أَنَّ التصديق أمر باطني لا اطلاع لغير الله وصاحبه عليه، وعلى هذا يكون مَن صدَّقَ بقلبه وترك الإقرار بلسانه - مع قدرته على الإقرار وتمكنه منه ـ مؤمنا فيما بينه وبين تعالى ، ويكون مقره الجنَّة ، ولكن كمال الدين بن الهمام ذكر أنَّ أهل هذا القول اتفقوا على أنَّ هذا المُصدِّق يلزمه أن يعتقد أنه متى طُلب منه الإقرار أتى به ، فإن طُولبَ ولمْ يُقرّ فهو بسبب كافر معاند .
وذهب أبو حنيفة [؟] إلى أن مناط الأحكام الأخروية الإقرار باللسان ، وما الأخرس [؟] في حكمه كإشارة ; فالمُصدِّقُ بقلبه الذي لم يُقرَّ بلسانه يكون مؤمناً ، ولكن إيمانه هذا لا تترتب عليه الأحكام الأخروية، ولعلَّ وجه ما ذهب هؤلاء إليه : أنه الله ذم المعاندين بأكثر مما ذم به الجاهلين المقصرين، ولقائل أن يقول: إن الذَّمَّ لأنهم أبوا أن يقروا بألسنتهم ؛ وذلك علامة التكذيب، أو لأنهم أنكروا بقلوبهم، وذلك هو التكذيب عينه، وحاصل ذلك منع وجود التصديق عند المعاند الذي تعلَّق الذَّمُّ به ; لأنَّ التصديق الذي يُعدُّ صاحبه مؤمنا هو ضد الإنكار ، وأمَّا الحاصل عند المُعاند المذموم فهو التصديق بمعنى المعرفة التي هي ضد النكارة والجهالة .
Statement of the reality of iman. Iman in language means tasdiq (affirmation), and the meaning of tasdiq is submission to the judgment and acceptance of it and admission of its truthfulness, and its origin is (al-amn) which is the opposite of fear, as if the reality of our saying 'so-and-so believed' is that he removed from himself the fear of being contradicted and opposed. As for iman in the technical sense of the people of the Sharia, the scholars have differed in defining it on five opinions: The first - and it is the madhhab of the majority of the investigators of the Ash'aris and Maturidis - that it is tasdiq of what is known to have come from the Prophet necessarily, in detail regarding what is known in detail, and in total regarding what is known in total. And despite their agreement that the reality of iman is only what we mentioned, they differed concerning the criterion of the rulings of the Hereafter: is it merely this tasdiq or is it with verbal iqrar (declaration)? And it is well known that al-Ash'ari and his followers say that this is the reality of iman, and this reality alone is the criterion for applying the rulings of the Hereafter, and iqrar is only required in their view so that people may know through it the existence of iman in its possessor and so that they may apply to him the rulings of this world; because tasdiq is an inward matter that no one besides Allah and its possessor is aware of. On this basis, whoever affirms with his heart and leaves out iqrar with his tongue - while being able to pronounce it and possessing the ability to do so - is a believer (mu'min) between himself and the Most High, and his abode is Paradise. However, Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam mentioned that the proponents of this view agreed that this affirmer must believe that when he is asked to pronounce iqrar he will do so; if he is demanded and does not pronounce it, then he is, due to that, a disbelieving obstinate (kafir mu'anid). Abu Hanifa [?] held that the criterion of the rulings of the Hereafter is verbal iqrar, and the mute [?] is regarded in his ruling like a gesture. So the one who affirms with his heart and does not pronounce with his tongue is a believer, but his iman does not result in the rulings of the Hereafter. Possibly the reason for what these [scholars] adopted is that Allah condemned the obstinate more severely than He condemned the ignorant shortcomers. And one might say: The condemnation is because they refused to pronounce with their tongues; and that is a sign of denial, or because they denied in their hearts, and that is the very denial. The upshot of that is the negation of the existence of tasdiq in the obstinate to whom condemnation is attached; because tasdiq that makes its possessor a believer is the opposite of denial, whereas what occurs in the condemned obstinate is tasdiq in the sense of recognition (ma'rifa) which is the opposite of unfamiliarity (nakara) and ignorance.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage defines iman both linguistically and in the Sharia, then presents the first madhhab (the majority of Ash'aris and Maturidis) and a debate about the role of iqrar. The author begins by explaining that linguistically iman means tasdiq (affirmation), which is acceptance and admission of truth. Its root is 'amn (security). In Sharia, scholars have five views. The first view is that iman is tasdiq of what the Prophet brought, either in detail or in general. The majority agree on this reality but differ on the criterion for the Hereafter: is it just tasdiq or tasdiq plus iqrar? Al-Ash'ari and followers hold that iman alone is tasdiq in the heart, and iqrar is only for worldly rulings. Thus a heart-believer who can but does not pronounce is still a believer in the Hereafter. However, Ibn al-Humam added that such a person must be willing to pronounce if asked; otherwise he is a kafir mu'anid (obstinate disbeliever). Then the author mentions the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) that iqrar is the criterion for the Hereafter, with a gesture for the mute. The debate is examined: why does Allah condemn obstinate people more? Some say their condemnation is due to their refusal to pronounce iqrar (a sign of denial), others say it is due to heart denial. The author concludes that the obstinate person does not have the tasdiq that counts as iman; rather he has mere ma'rifa (recognition), which is not enough.

Iman in Arabic means tasdiq (affirmation) derived from 'amn (security), signifying acceptance that removes fear of denial.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?
If iman is not just intellectual belief but active submission and acceptance, what is one area of your life where you have not yet fully submitted to Allah's judgment? What is holding you back from that surrender?

The First Madhhab on Iman and the Role of Iqrar
First madhhab definition of iman and the iqrar debate.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the Ash'ari/Maturidi definition of iman and the debate over whether iqrar (verbal declaration) is required for salvation.

Core Idea
For Ash'aris, iman is heart affirmation; iqrar is only for worldly rulings.

After the linguistic foundation, Sanusi moves to the Shar'i definition, where scholars differ. The first madhhab—the majority of Ash'aris and Maturidis—defines iman as tasdiq of what the Prophet brought. But a key debate emerges: is iqrar part of iman's reality or just a worldly requirement? This lesson explores that dispute and its implications for salvation.

Guided Path
1
Understand the basic definition
Read the passage where Sanusi states the first madhhab: iman is tasdiq of known prophetic teachings, in detail or general. Note that this is the consensus of Ash'aris and Maturidis.
The definition distinguishes between detailed and general knowledge.
2
Follow the debate on iqrar
The text explains that despite agreeing on the reality, scholars differed on whether iqrar is needed for the Hereafter. Identify the two positions: Ash'ari (tasdiq alone) and Hanafi (iqrar required).
Look for the phrase 'أنَّ الأشعري وأتباعه يقولون'.
3
Examine the obstinate case
Read about the obstinate person (mu'anid) who has tasdiq but refuses to declare. Note how Ibn al-Humam adds a condition, and how the Hanafis use Qur'anic condemnation to argue for iqrar being essential.
The passage concludes that the obstinate only has ma'rifa (recognition), not true tasdiq.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حقيقة الإيمان
الإيمان في اللغة معناه : التصديق ، ومعنى التصديق : الإذعان للحكم وقبوله والاعتراف بكونه صادقا، والأصل فيه: (الأمن) الذي هو ضد الخوف ، وكأنَّ حقيقة قولنا: «آمن فلان» أنه نفى عنه خوف التكذيب والمخالفة .
وأما الإيمان في عرف أهل الشرع فقد اختلف العلماء في تحديد معناه على خمسة أقوال: أولها - وهو مذهب جمهور المحققين من الأشاعرة والماتريدية ـ أنَّه : التصديق بما عُلم مجيء النبي به ضرورة تفصيلا فيما عُلم تفصيلا، وإجمالا فيما عُلم إجمالاً ، ومع اتفاقهم على أنَّ حقيقة الإيمان هي ما ذكرنا فحسب اختلفوا في مناط أحكام الآخرة: أهو مجرد هذا التصديق أم هو مع الإقرار باللسان ؟ وقد اشتهر أنَّ الأشعري وأتباعه يقولون: إن هذه هي حقيقة الإيمان، وهذه الحقيقة وحدها هي مناط إجراء أحكام الآخرة، والإقرار إنما يشترط عندهم ليعرف الناس به وجودَ الإيمان عند صاحبه وليُجروا عليه أحكام الدُّنيا ; أَنَّ التصديق أمر باطني لا اطلاع لغير الله وصاحبه عليه، وعلى هذا يكون مَن صدَّقَ بقلبه وترك الإقرار بلسانه - مع قدرته على الإقرار وتمكنه منه ـ مؤمنا فيما بينه وبين تعالى ، ويكون مقره الجنَّة ، ولكن كمال الدين بن الهمام ذكر أنَّ أهل هذا القول اتفقوا على أنَّ هذا المُصدِّق يلزمه أن يعتقد أنه متى طُلب منه الإقرار أتى به ، فإن طُولبَ ولمْ يُقرّ فهو بسبب كافر معاند .
وذهب أبو حنيفة [؟] إلى أن مناط الأحكام الأخروية الإقرار باللسان ، وما الأخرس [؟] في حكمه كإشارة ; فالمُصدِّقُ بقلبه الذي لم يُقرَّ بلسانه يكون مؤمناً ، ولكن إيمانه هذا لا تترتب عليه الأحكام الأخروية، ولعلَّ وجه ما ذهب هؤلاء إليه : أنه الله ذم المعاندين بأكثر مما ذم به الجاهلين المقصرين، ولقائل أن يقول: إن الذَّمَّ لأنهم أبوا أن يقروا بألسنتهم ؛ وذلك علامة التكذيب، أو لأنهم أنكروا بقلوبهم، وذلك هو التكذيب عينه، وحاصل ذلك منع وجود التصديق عند المعاند الذي تعلَّق الذَّمُّ به ; لأنَّ التصديق الذي يُعدُّ صاحبه مؤمنا هو ضد الإنكار ، وأمَّا الحاصل عند المُعاند المذموم فهو التصديق بمعنى المعرفة التي هي ضد النكارة والجهالة .
Statement of the reality of iman. Iman in language means tasdiq (affirmation), and the meaning of tasdiq is submission to the judgment and acceptance of it and admission of its truthfulness, and its origin is (al-amn) which is the opposite of fear, as if the reality of our saying 'so-and-so believed' is that he removed from himself the fear of being contradicted and opposed. As for iman in the technical sense of the people of the Sharia, the scholars have differed in defining it on five opinions: The first - and it is the madhhab of the majority of the investigators of the Ash'aris and Maturidis - that it is tasdiq of what is known to have come from the Prophet necessarily, in detail regarding what is known in detail, and in total regarding what is known in total. And despite their agreement that the reality of iman is only what we mentioned, they differed concerning the criterion of the rulings of the Hereafter: is it merely this tasdiq or is it with verbal iqrar (declaration)? And it is well known that al-Ash'ari and his followers say that this is the reality of iman, and this reality alone is the criterion for applying the rulings of the Hereafter, and iqrar is only required in their view so that people may know through it the existence of iman in its possessor and so that they may apply to him the rulings of this world; because tasdiq is an inward matter that no one besides Allah and its possessor is aware of. On this basis, whoever affirms with his heart and leaves out iqrar with his tongue - while being able to pronounce it and possessing the ability to do so - is a believer (mu'min) between himself and the Most High, and his abode is Paradise. However, Kamal al-Din ibn al-Humam mentioned that the proponents of this view agreed that this affirmer must believe that when he is asked to pronounce iqrar he will do so; if he is demanded and does not pronounce it, then he is, due to that, a disbelieving obstinate (kafir mu'anid). Abu Hanifa [?] held that the criterion of the rulings of the Hereafter is verbal iqrar, and the mute [?] is regarded in his ruling like a gesture. So the one who affirms with his heart and does not pronounce with his tongue is a believer, but his iman does not result in the rulings of the Hereafter. Possibly the reason for what these [scholars] adopted is that Allah condemned the obstinate more severely than He condemned the ignorant shortcomers. And one might say: The condemnation is because they refused to pronounce with their tongues; and that is a sign of denial, or because they denied in their hearts, and that is the very denial. The upshot of that is the negation of the existence of tasdiq in the obstinate to whom condemnation is attached; because tasdiq that makes its possessor a believer is the opposite of denial, whereas what occurs in the condemned obstinate is tasdiq in the sense of recognition (ma'rifa) which is the opposite of unfamiliarity (nakara) and ignorance.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage defines iman both linguistically and in the Sharia, then presents the first madhhab (the majority of Ash'aris and Maturidis) and a debate about the role of iqrar. The author begins by explaining that linguistically iman means tasdiq (affirmation), which is acceptance and admission of truth. Its root is 'amn (security). In Sharia, scholars have five views. The first view is that iman is tasdiq of what the Prophet brought, either in detail or in general. The majority agree on this reality but differ on the criterion for the Hereafter: is it just tasdiq or tasdiq plus iqrar? Al-Ash'ari and followers hold that iman alone is tasdiq in the heart, and iqrar is only for worldly rulings. Thus a heart-believer who can but does not pronounce is still a believer in the Hereafter. However, Ibn al-Humam added that such a person must be willing to pronounce if asked; otherwise he is a kafir mu'anid (obstinate disbeliever). Then the author mentions the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) that iqrar is the criterion for the Hereafter, with a gesture for the mute. The debate is examined: why does Allah condemn obstinate people more? Some say their condemnation is due to their refusal to pronounce iqrar (a sign of denial), others say it is due to heart denial. The author concludes that the obstinate person does not have the tasdiq that counts as iman; rather he has mere ma'rifa (recognition), which is not enough.

Four Additional Definitions of Iman
Sanusi enumerates four definitions of iman and states his preference.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the four additional sectarian definitions of iman and why the Ash'ari/Maturidi view of tasdiq alone is preferred.

Core Idea
Four contested definitions of iman; the only sound one is tasdiq of the heart.

Imam Sanusi continues his survey of definitions of iman, presenting four more views from the Karramites, Khawarij, Mu'tazila, and a combined view from some Ahl al-Sunna and Ahl al-Hadith. Each reduces iman to a different combination of speech, action, or belief. After listing them, Sanusi states his own conviction: the soul rests only on the first view that iman is tasdiq alone, as affirmed by the Ash'ari and Maturidi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Read the four definitions
Read the Arabic passage carefully. Notice the numbering: second, third, fourth, fifth. Each is a separate madhhab with a distinct definition of iman.
The first madhhab (tasdiq alone) was covered in the previous lesson.
2
Compare the components
For each madhhab, identify which components of iman are included: verbal declaration (iqrar), heart belief (tasdiq), and actions (obligatory or supererogatory).
The Karramites include only speech; the Khawarij include all actions; al-Jubba'i limits to obligatory acts; the fifth view combines heart, tongue, and limbs.
3
Analyze the concluding preference
Sanusi ends by stating that the soul is at ease with the first madhhab (tasdiq alone). Why does he reject the other four? Think about the principle of iman being inward and not subject to increase/decrease.
This preference sets up the proofs in the next lesson.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المذهب الثاني: - وهو مذهب الكرامية أنَّ الإيمان هو إقرار اللسان بالشهادتين لا غير
المذهب الثالث: - وهو مذهب الخوارج وجماعة من المعتزلة منهم العَلّاف وعبد الجبار أنَّ الإيمان هو الطاعات مطلقاً، سواء أكانت فروضاً أم كانت نوافل .
المذهب الرابع: - وهو مذهب الجُبَّائي وابنه وأكثر معتزلة البصرة أنَّ الإيمان هو الطَّاعات المفترضة دون النوافل .
المذهب الخامس: - وهو مذهب جماعةٍ مِن أهل السُّنَّة القَلَانِسي وجماعة من المعتزلة النجار ، وهو أيضاً مذهب الكثيرين من أهل الحديث - أنَّ الإيمان هو التصديق بالجنان ، والإقرار باللسان والعمل بالأركان، والجنان - بفتح الجيم - القلب، والأركان ههنا بمعنى الجوارح. والذي تطمئن إليه النفس من هذه المذاهب : أنَّ الإيمان هو التصديق وحده كما ذهب إليه محققو الأشاعرة والماتريدية.
The second madhhab: It is the madhhab of the Karramites that iman is pronunciation of the two shahadahs by the tongue and nothing else. The third madhhab: It is the madhhab of the Khawarij and a group of the Mu'tazila, among them al-Allaf and Abd al-Jabbar, that iman is acts of obedience absolutely, whether they be obligatory or supererogatory. The fourth madhhab: It is the madhhab of al-Jubba'i, his son (Abu Hashim), and most of the Basran Mu'tazila that iman is obligatory acts of obedience without the supererogatory. The fifth madhhab: It is the madhhab of a group from the Ahl al-Sunna, al-Qalanisi, and a group of the Mu'tazila, al-Najjar, and it is also the madhhab of many from the Ahl al-Hadith - that iman is tasdiq with the heart (jinan), iqrar with the tongue, and action with the limbs (arkan). Jinan - with fath of the jim - is the heart, and arkan here means the physical limbs. And that which the soul is at ease with among these madhahib is that iman is tasdiq alone as held by the investigators of the Ash'aris and Maturidis.
Source pages p. 177

Commentary
This passage lists four additional madhahib on the definition of iman. The second madhhab (Karamites) says iman is only the verbal declaration of the two shahadahs. The third (Khawarij and some Mu'tazila like al-Allaf and Abd al-Jabbar) says iman is all acts of obedience, both obligatory and supererogatory. The fourth (al-Jubba'i, his son, and most Basran Mu'tazila) restricts it to obligatory acts only. The fifth (a group of Ahl al-Sunna, al-Qalanisi, some Mu'tazila like al-Najjar, and many Ahl al-Hadith) combines tasdiq with the heart, iqrar with the tongue, and action with the limbs. After listing these, the author states his preference: the soul is at ease with the first madhhab (Ash'ari/Maturidi) that iman is tasdiq alone. This preference is the transition to the next lesson's proofs.

Key Takeaway

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?

?

?

Three Schools on the Definition of Iman
Al-Laqqani enumerates three theological schools on the definition of iman and states his preferred view.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand three major theological schools on the definition of faith (iman) and the preferred Ash'ari-Maturidi view.

Core Idea
Iman can be defined as acts, words, or heart attestation — but the soundest view is tasdiq alone.

In this passage, al-Laqqani presents three distinct positions on the reality of faith (iman), each representing a major theological school. After laying out these views, he states his own preference — the position of the verifying scholars among the Ash'aris and Maturidis. This lesson will help you navigate these definitions and understand why the heart's attestation is considered the core of faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the Arabic passage and translation
Read the Arabic passage once without trying to analyse it. Then read the translation. Let the author's own rhythm come through before you interpret.
2
Identify the third, fourth, and fifth schools
The passage presents three schools on iman. For each, note the definition given: what does that school hold faith to be?
3
Note the author's preferred view
After listing the schools, al-Laqqani states which view he finds most reassuring. Identify that view and the groups associated with it.
4
Discuss the common misunderstanding
The passage only mentions three schools, not all five. Avoid assuming these are the only definitions; earlier schools (first and second) are not covered here.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان حقيقة الإيمان المذهب الثالث: - وهو مذهب الخوارج وجماعة من المعتزلة منهم العلاف وعبد الجبار ـ أنَّ الإيمان هو الطاعات مطلقاً، سواء أكانت فروضاً أم كانت نوافل . - المذهب الرابع: - وهو مذهب الجُبَّائي وابنه وأكثر معتزلة البصرة ـ أن الإيمان هو الطَّاعات المفترضة دون النوافل . المذهب الخامس: - وهو مذهب جماعةٍ مِن أهل السُّنَّة القَلَانِسي وجماعة من المعتزلة النجار ، وهو أيضاً مذهب الكثيرين من أهل الحديث - أنَّ الإيمان هو التصديق بالجنان ، والإقرار باللسان والعمل بالأركان، والجنان - بفتح الجيم - القلب، والأركان ههنا بمعنى الجوارح. والذي تطمئن إليه النفس من هذه المذاهب : أنَّ الإيمان هو التصديق وحده كما ذهب إليه محققو الأشاعرة والماتريدية.
Statement of the Reality of Faith. The third school: - which is the school of the Khawarij and a group of the Mu'tazila, among them al-'Allaf and 'Abd al-Jabbar - that faith (iman) is all acts of obedience, whether obligatory or supererogatory. - The fourth school: - which is the school of al-Jubba'i and his son and most of the Mu'tazila of Basra - that faith is obligatory acts of obedience, not supererogatory. The fifth school: - which is the school of a group of Ahl al-Sunnah, al-Qalanisi, and a group of the Mu'tazila, al-Najjar, and it is also the school of many of the People of Hadith - that faith is attestation (tasdiq) by the heart (jinan), verbal confession (iqrar) by the tongue, and action ('amal) by the limbs (arkan). Al-Jinan - with a fath on the jim - is the heart, and al-arkan here means the limbs. And that which the soul feels reassured by among these schools is that faith is attestation alone, as held by the verifying scholars of the Ash'aris and Maturidis.
Source pages p. 178

Commentary
This passage is an enumeration. The author lists three schools (the third, fourth, and fifth) on the definition of iman. The third school (Khawarij and some Mu'tazila) holds that iman is all acts of obedience, obligatory and supererogatory. The fourth school (al-Jubba'i and his son, and most Basran Mu'tazila) restricts iman to obligatory acts only. The fifth school (a group of Ahl al-Sunnah, al-Qalanisi, and some Mu'tazila) defines iman as comprising three elements: heart attestation (tasdiq bil-jinan), tongue confession (iqrar bil-lisan), and limb action ('amal bil-arkan). The author then declares his own preference: the view that iman is solely tasdiq (attestation) in the heart, which is the position of the verifying scholars among the Ash'aris and Maturidis. Note that the first two schools are not mentioned here, presumably covered earlier. The author does not argue for his preference here; he merely states it.

5 min
The True Meaning of Affirming the Prophet
Sanusi defines tasdiq of the Prophet as acceptance with satisfaction and action.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that true affirmation (tasdiq) of the Prophet requires acceptance, satisfaction, and action, not mere mental acknowledgment.

Core Idea
True affirmation demands submission and deeds, not just knowledge.

Sanusi begins by clarifying what it truly means to affirm the Prophet. He warns against a shallow understanding that would wrongly count many disbelievers as believers. This passage establishes the central role of submission and action in genuine faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the passage carefully
Read the Arabic and translation, noting how Sanusi defines tasdiq as acceptance with satisfaction and building deeds, contrasting it with mere mental attribution of truth.
Pay attention to the contrast between 'إذعان' and 'مجرد وقوع نسبة الصدق'.
2
Identify the key contrast
Find where Sanusi says what tasdiq is NOT: 'لا مجرد وقوع نسبة الصدق إليه في القلب من غير إذعان وقبول له'. Understand the implication: mere belief without submission is insufficient.
He uses disbelievers who knew the truth as proof.
3
Reflect on the consequence
Consider why this matters: if mere belief were enough, many disbelievers would be considered believers. This shows faith requires the heart's submission and actions, not just cognition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمراد من تصديقه (١) صلى الله عليه وسلم : قبول ما جاءَ به مع الرّضا بترك التكبر والعِناد ؛ وبناء الأعمال (٢) عليه ، لا مجرَّد وقوع نسبة الصدق إليه في القلب من غير إذعان وقبول له ، حتّى يلزمَ الحُكْم بإيمان كثير من الكفَّار الذين كانوا عالمين بحقيَّة نبوته هو ما جاء به ؛ لأنَّهم لم يكونوا أَذْعنوا لذلك ولا قَبلُوه ولا بنوا الأعمال الصَّالحة عليه ، بحيثُ صارَ يُطلق عليه اسم التسليم كما هو مدلوله الوضعي ؛ لأنَّ حقيقة آمن به آمَنَهُ التَّكذِيبَ والمُخالفة وجَعَلَهُ في من ذلك. أمن النطق بالشهادتين والخلاف فيه هل هو شرط للإيمان أو شطر فيه ] ولما اختلف العلماء في جهة مدخليّة النُّطق بالشهادتين في حقيقة (١) قد عرفت مما حررناه لك في أثناء شرح المذهب الأوَّل من مذاهب العلماء في بيان حقيقة الإيمان الشرعية أنَّ التصديق يطلق على معنيين: أحدهما: الجزم والقطع بالشيء بحيث لا يكون عند صاحبه شيء من التردد والحيرة والشك ، وهذا هو المعنى الذي يُعبّر العلماء عنه بالإذعان، ويقابله بهذا المعنى الإنكار ، ولا شك أنَّ هذا المعنى متى وجد عند شخص كان قابلا لما صَدَّقَ به راضياً به تاركاً لكل ما يناقضه ، وإلا لم يكن مُصدقًا بهذا المعنى ضرورة أنَّ العاقل يسير على وفق ما أداه إليه نظره وأذعن له فكره وسلم به عقله . والمعنى الثاني من معاني التصديق المعرفة المجردة عن الإذعان والجزم، وهذه المعرفة هي المقابلة للجهالة والنكارة، والتصديق بهذا المعنى كان موجودا عند كثير من الكفار وأهل الكتاب الذين لم يؤمنوا بما جاء به الرسول صلى الله عليه وسلم ، وآية ذلك قوله : ﴿فَلَمَّا جَاءَهُم مَّا عَرَفُوا كَفَرُوا بوء ﴾ [البقرة: (٨٩] فدل على أنَّ التصديق بهذا المعنى لا يستلزم إذعان المُصدِّقِ لما عرفه ولا انقياده له ولا تسليمه به ولا أن يترك ما يناقضه . محي.
And what is meant by his affirmation (tasdiq), may Allah bless him and grant him peace: acceptance of what he brought with satisfaction, leaving aside arrogance and obstinacy; and building righteous deeds upon it, not merely the occurrence of the attribution of truthfulness to him in the heart without submission (idh'aan) and acceptance, such that it would necessitate the judgment of faith for many of the disbelievers who knew the reality of his prophethood and what he brought; because they did not submit to it, nor accept it, nor build righteous deeds upon it, such that the name 'submission' (taslim) is applied to him according to its conventional meaning. For the reality of 'amana bihi' is that he grants him security from denial and opposition and makes him... from that. Is the utterance of the two testimonies and the dispute concerning it whether it is a condition (shart) of faith or a part (shitr) of it? And since the scholars differed concerning the aspect of the involvement of the utterance of the two testimonies in the reality... (1) You have known from what we have written for you during the explanation of the first school of thought concerning the legal reality of faith that affirmation (tasdiq) is used in two senses: one of them: certainty and decisiveness about a thing such that nothing of hesitation, confusion, or doubt is present with its possessor; this is the meaning that scholars express as submission (idh'aan), and its opposite in this sense is denial (inkaar). There is no doubt that when this meaning is present in a person, he is accepting of what he affirms, satisfied with it, abandoning everything that contradicts it; otherwise he is not a true affirmer in this sense, necessarily because the rational person proceeds according to what his reflection leads him to, his mind submits to, and his intellect accepts. The second meaning of affirmation is mere cognition (ma'rifa) stripped of submission and certainty; this cognition is the opposite of ignorance and denial. Affirmation in this sense was present among many disbelievers and People of the Book who did not believe in what the Messenger, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, brought. Evidence for that is His saying: {But when there came to them that which they recognized, they disbelieved in it} [al-Baqara: 89]. So it indicates that affirmation in this sense does not necessitate the affirmer's submission to what he knows, nor his compliance with it, nor his acceptance of it, nor that he abandon what contradicts it.
Source pages p. 183

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the term 'tasdiq' (affirmation) as it relates to faith in the Messenger. The author begins by stating what is meant by affirming the Prophet: it is the acceptance of what he brought, accompanied by satisfaction and abandonment of arrogance and obstinacy, and building righteous deeds upon it. He contrasts this with merely holding a belief that the Prophet is truthful in one's heart without submission and acceptance. If mere belief sufficed, then many disbelievers who knew the truth of his prophethood would be considered believers, which is false. Such disbelievers did not submit to or accept his message, nor did they base their deeds upon it. Thus the term 'taslim' (submission) is applied to true affirmation in its conventional sense. Then the author transitions to the issue of the utterance of the two testimonies, whether it is a condition or a part of faith. In the following footnote, the author explains that he has previously established that 'tasdiq' has two meanings. The first meaning is decisive certainty (jazm) that leaves no room for hesitation or doubt; scholars call this 'idh'aan' (submission). When this meaning is present, the person necessarily accepts and is satisfied with what he affirms and abandons all that contradicts it. The second meaning is mere cognition (ma'rifa) stripped of submission and certainty; this is simply the opposite of ignorance. This second meaning of 'tasdiq' was present in many disbelievers and People of the Book who did not believe in the Prophet. The author cites Quran 2:89 as evidence: they recognized the truth but disbelieved out of arrogance. Therefore, this type of affirmation does not entail submission, compliance, or abandonment of contradicting beliefs.

Key Terms
تصديق
إذعان
تسليم
إنكار

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: Some think that simply believing the Prophet is truthful is enough for faith.
Correction: True faith requires acceptance with satisfaction, abandoning arrogance, and building deeds upon that belief.

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what distinguishes true affirmation from mere mental assent?
A) It involves doubt about the message.
B) It includes acceptance, satisfaction, and building deeds.
C) It requires verbal declaration only.
D) It is only for the Prophet's companions.

Key Takeaway
True affirmation of the Prophet is not just belief in his truthfulness but requires submission, acceptance, and actions that flow from it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Is there a teaching of the Prophet (ﷺ) that you intellectually accept but have not truly submitted to, still feeling a sense of pride or resistance? What would it take for you to abandon that arrogance and embrace it with satisfaction?
?
Think of a specific command from the Sunnah that you know is true but have not consistently acted upon. What would need to change in your heart for you to build your deeds upon it rather than just acknowledging it?
?
When you recite the shahadah, do you feel that you are granting the Prophet (ﷺ) security from denial in your life, or do you sometimes oppose his teachings to follow your own desires? How can you make your 'amana bihi' more complete today?

What Is Kalam?
intermediate
6 min
Two Meanings of Tasdiq: Certainty vs. Cognition
Sanusi explains the two meanings of tasdiq and their contrasting implications for faith.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand that tasdiq has two distinct meanings: decisive certainty (jazm/idh'aan) and mere cognition (ma'rifa), and only the first constitutes true faith.

Core Idea
Affirmation can mean either full submission or mere recognition; only the first saves.

In this footnote, Sanusi elaborates on two meanings of tasdiq that scholars have distinguished. The first is firm conviction that leads to acceptance and action, while the second is mere knowledge without submission. He cites the Quran to show that many disbelievers possessed the second but not the first, proving that mere cognition is insufficient for faith.

Guided Path
1
Read the footnote passage
Read the Arabic and translation. Notice that Sanusi explicitly states tasdiq is used in two senses.
The first sense is jazm (certainty) and idh'aan (submission); the second is ma'rifa (cognition).
2
Analyze the first meaning
Identify how Sanusi describes the first meaning: certain conviction leaving no room for doubt, and it necessarily leads to acceptance and action. The rational person acts according to what his mind submits to.
This meaning corresponds to true faith.
3
Analyze the second meaning
The second meaning is mere knowledge without submission or certainty. It is simply the opposite of ignorance. Sanusi says this was present in many disbelievers and People of the Book.
He uses Quran 2:89 as evidence: they recognized the truth but rejected it.
4
Understand the implication
The second meaning does not lead to submission, compliance, or abandoning contradictory beliefs. Therefore, it does not constitute faith.
This clarifies why some disbelievers had knowledge but were not believers.

⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

Commentary
This passage is a definition and explanation of the term 'tasdiq' (affirmation) as it relates to faith in the Messenger. This second meaning of 'tasdiq' was present in many disbelievers and People of the Book who did not believe in the Prophet. The author cites Quran 2:89 as evidence: they recognized the truth but disbelieved out of arrogance. Therefore, this type of affirmation does not entail submission, compliance, or abandonment of contradicting beliefs.

Misconception: Some think that having knowledge of Islam's truth is enough to be a believer.

Checkpoint
What is the evidence Sanusi gives that the second meaning of tasdiq existed in disbelievers?
A) Their belief in one God.
B) Their rejection of the Prophet out of envy.
C) Quran 2:89: they recognized the truth but disbelieved.
D) Their performance of some rituals.

Key Takeaway
The decisive meaning of tasdiq for faith is certainty with submission; mere cognition, though it is a form of affirmation, is insufficient for true belief.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Are you certain of the truths of faith—like the Qur'an being from Allah—in the first sense (with no hesitation), or do you only recognize them intellectually like those who disbelieved despite knowing? What would change if you moved from recognition to certainty?
?
The passage says the rational person acts according to what his reflection leads him to. Look at your life: where do you act against what you claim to believe? What does that say about the reality of your tasdiq?
?
If mere cognition is not enough for salvation, then your knowledge of Islam is not enough. Have you submitted your entire being to what you know? What one area of your life remains unsurrendered, and what is holding you back?

What Is Kalam?
beginner
5 min
Definition of the Psychic Attribute
Defines the psychic attribute with commentary and examples.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the definition of the psychic attribute as a positive attribute that indicates the essence itself without any additional meaning, and you will recognize its examples.

Core Idea
The psychic attribute points to the essence, not to any extra quality.

This lesson introduces a foundational concept in Islamic theology: the psychic attribute (al-sifa al-nafsiyya). This category describes attributes that tell us about the essence directly, without implying any added characteristic. Grasping this concept is essential for understanding how theologians speak about God's attributes, especially existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition carefully
Read the Arabic definition of the psychic attribute. Notice the key phrase 'without an additional meaning' (دون معنى زائد عليها). This is the defining characteristic.
The term 'psychic' here means 'pertaining to the essence' (nafs).
2
Study the commentary notes
Examine the two commentary notes by al-Shanwani. The first clarifies that 'without an additional meaning' is synonymous with 'upon the essence itself'. The second explains that the examples apply to both originated and eternal beings.
This shows the definition is general.
3
Identify the examples
List the examples given: a substance being a substance, an essence, a thing, and an existent. Understand that each of these descriptions refers to the essence without adding extra content.
These examples help illustrate the concept.
4
Connect to the broader context
Ask yourself why this classification matters. In kalam, psychic attributes are contrasted with attributes that add meaning. This distinction becomes important when discussing God's existence.
This lesson sets the stage for the next one.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
القسم الأول: الصفة النفسية
[ تعريف الصفة النفسية
والمراد بالصّفة النّفسيَّة: صفةٌ ثبوتيَّةٌ يدلُّ الوصف بها على نفس الذات دون معنى زائد عليها، ككون الجوهر جوهرا، وذاتا، وشيئا، وموجودا.
(۱) قوله: (دون معنى زائد عليها) تفسير مرادف لقوله: (على نفس الذات) أي: أن معنى دلالتها على نفس الذات أنها لا تدل على شيء زائد عليها؛ فلذلك سميت نفسية. الشنواني.
(۲) قوله: (ككون الجوهر جوهرا ... الخ) هذا تمثيل للصفة النفسية، لأن التعريف للصفة النفسية مطلقا؛ حادثة كانت أو قديمة. الشنواني.
(۳) القول في الوجود يحتاج إلى بيان ثلاثة أمور: الأول: معنى الوجود، والثاني: معنى وجوبه له سبحانه، والثالث: الدليل على وجوب وجود الله تعالى. فأما الكلام على الأول فيستدعي أن نُقدّم لك بحثًا يترتب عليه بيان معنى الوجود، وهذا البحث يتلخص في أنَّ الوجود مطلقا ـ نعني سواء أكان صفةٌ للقديم أم كان صفة للحادث - هل هو عين الذات الموجودة أو هو غير الذات؟ وقد اختلف العلماء في هذه المسألة، فذهب أبو الحسن الأشعري: إلى أن الوجود هو نفس الذات، وعلى هذا لا يقال إن الوجود صفة، لأن الصفة اسم للأمر الزائد على الموصوف، وعلى هذا يكون عد المتكلمين والمؤلفين المصنف والشارح الوجود من الصفات الواجبة له سبحانه مشتملا على شيء من التّسامح، وسببه: أنهم رأوا أنه يصح وصف ذات الله تعالى لفظا بما يُشتق من الوجود، فيقال: «ذات الله موجودة» فلما رأوا أنَّ الوجود يكون وصفًا في اللفظ كالصفة الحقيقية في نحو قولنا: الله تعالى عالم وقادر أطلقوا لفظ الصفة على الوجود تشبيها له بها. وقال قوم منهم الرَّازِيُّ: الوجود أمر زائد على الذات، على معنى أنه صفة ثابتة في الخارج لكنها لم تصل إلى درجة الموجودات التي تشاهد وتحسُّ، فهي واسطة بين الموجود الخارجي والمعدوم، وهذا الفريق أثبت واسطة بين الموجود والمعدوم، وسمّي هذه الواسطة عنده ثلاثة: معدوم، وموجود، وحالٌ. أما الفريق الأول فليس عنده إلا حالا، فالأقسام قسمان: الموجود والمعدوم.
The first section: The psychic attribute. [Definition of the psychic attribute: And what is meant by the psychic attribute is: a positive attribute whose description indicates the essence itself without an additional meaning, such as the substance being a substance, an essence, a thing, and an existent. (1) His statement: (without an additional meaning) is an explanatory synonym for his statement: (upon the essence itself), meaning that the meaning of its indication upon the essence itself is that it does not indicate something additional to it; therefore it is called psychic. Al-Shanwani. (2) His statement: (such as the substance being a substance... etc.) This is an example of the psychic attribute, because the definition of the psychic attribute is absolute, whether it is originated or eternal. Al-Shanwani. (3) The discussion on existence requires clarification of three matters: First: the meaning of existence, Second: the meaning of its necessity for Him, exalted, and Third: the proof for the necessity of the existence of Allah, exalted. As for speaking on the first, it requires that we present to you an investigation upon which the clarification of the meaning of existence depends, and this investigation is summarized in that existence absolutely — meaning whether it be an attribute of the eternal or an attribute of the originated — is it identical to the existing essence or is it other than the essence? And the scholars have differed in this issue: Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari held that existence is identical to the essence, and on this basis it is not said that existence is an attribute, because an attribute is a name for something additional to the described. On this basis, the enumeration by the theologians and authors — the author and the commentator — of existence among the necessary attributes of Him, exalted, involves some indulgence. The reason is that they saw that it is valid to describe the essence of Allah, exalted, verbally with what is derived from existence, so it is said: 'The essence of Allah is existent.' So when they saw that existence is a description in speech like a real attribute in something like our saying: Allah, exalted, is knowing and powerful, they applied the term 'attribute' to existence by analogy with it. And some people, among them al-Razi, said: Existence is something additional to the essence, meaning that it is an attribute established in the external world but it has not reached the level of existents that are observed and sensed; it is an intermediary between the external existent and the non-existent. This group affirmed an intermediary between the existent and the non-existent, and they named this intermediary three: non-existent, existent, and state (hal). As for the first group, they have only two: for them, the divisions are two: the existent and the non-existent.
Source pages p. 214

Commentary
This passage begins by defining the psychic attribute (al-sifa al-nafsiyya). It is a positive attribute (sifa thubutiyya) that indicates the essence itself without any additional meaning. Examples include the substance being a substance, an essence, a thing, and an existent. The commentary by al-Shanwani clarifies that 'without an additional meaning' is synonymous with 'upon the essence itself,' and the examples apply whether the attribute is originated (haditha) or eternal (qadima). The passage then transitions to a discussion on existence (al-wujud), which is a major topic. It outlines three matters: the meaning of existence, the meaning of its necessity for God, and the proof for God's necessary existence. The central question is whether existence is identical to the essence or additional. Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari held that existence is identical to the essence; thus existence is not a real attribute but sometimes called an attribute by analogy. Al-Razi and others held that existence is an additional attribute, existing as an intermediary between existent and non-existent, calling it a 'state' (hal). The passage ends by noting the two groups' divisions: the first group only has existent and non-existent, while the second adds a third category of 'state.'

Key Terms
الصفة النفسية (al-sifa al-nafsiyya)
صفة ثبوتية (sifa thubutiyya)
عين الذات (ayn al-dhat)

Key Terms from Source Passage

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think the psychic attribute implies a real additional meaning beyond the essence.
Correction: The psychic attribute indicates nothing beyond the essence itself; it is a description of the essence without adding any extra characteristic.

Checkpoint
According to the definition, what does a psychic attribute indicate?
A) The essence itself without an additional meaning
B) The essence along with an additional meaning
C) Only the accidents of the essence
D) The non-existence of the essence

Key Takeaway
A psychic attribute describes the essence directly and adds no extra meaning beyond it.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you describe yourself to others, do you focus on essential qualities that truly define you, or do you add many extra labels that are not really you? Today, identify one attribute you claim that is actually accidental, and ask yourself why you hold onto it.
?
The definition of a psychic attribute applies to both created and eternal beings. When you think about your relationship with Allah, do you sometimes treat His attributes as if they were like your own - adding extra layers? How can you purify your understanding of Allah's names to reflect that they point directly to His essence without addition? Commit to studying one of His names with this awareness.

The Debate on Existence
Discusses the debate on existence and its relationship to the essence.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand the two positions on whether existence is identical to the essence or an additional attribute, and the implications for divine attributes.

Core Idea
Theologians disagree: for al-Ash'ari, existence is the essence itself; for al-Razi, it is an extra attribute.

The discussion on existence is central to understanding how God's existence is described. This lesson presents the key debate between Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari and Fakhr al-Din al-Razi. The passage outlines the three matters to be discussed about existence and then focuses on the first: whether existence is identical to the essence or additional.

Guided Path
1
Read the three matters
The passage begins by stating that the discussion on existence requires clarifying three matters: the meaning of existence, the meaning of its necessity for God, and the proof for God's necessary existence.
This lesson focuses on the first matter.
2
Identify the central question
The key question is whether existence is identical to the existing essence or something additional. Recognize that this is a dispute among theologians.
3
Study al-Ash'ari's view
According to al-Ash'ari, existence is identical to the essence. Therefore, existence is not a true attribute; calling it an attribute is a verbal analogy.
This view denies that existence is a real attribute.
4
Study al-Razi's view
Al-Razi holds that existence is an additional attribute, an intermediary between the existent and the non-existent, called a 'state' (hal).
This view posits three categories: existent, non-existent, and state.
5
Compare the divisions
Note that al-Ash'ari's group only has two divisions (existent and non-existent), while al-Razi's group adds a third (state).
This difference has implications for how attributes are classified.

القسم الأول: الصفة النفسية
[ تعريف الصفة النفسية
والمراد بالصّفة النّفسيَّة: صفةٌ ثبوتيَّةٌ يدلُّ الوصف بها على نفس الذات دون معنى زائد عليها، ككون الجوهر جوهرا، وذاتا، وشيئا، وموجودا.
(۱) قوله: (دون معنى زائد عليها) تفسير مرادف لقوله: (على نفس الذات) أي: أن معنى دلالتها على نفس الذات أنها لا تدل على شيء زائد عليها؛ فلذلك سميت نفسية. الشنواني.

(۳) القول في الوجود يحتاج إلى بيان ثلاثة أمور: الأول: معنى الوجود، والثاني: معنى وجوبه له سبحانه، والثالث: الدليل على وجوب وجود الله تعالى. فأما الكلام على الأول فيستدعي أن نُقدّم لك بحثًا يترتب عليه بيان معنى الوجود، وهذا البحث يتلخص في أنَّ الوجود مطلقا ـ نعني سواء أكان صفةٌ للقديم أم كان صفة للحادث - هل هو عين الذات الموجودة أو هو غير الذات؟ وقد اختلف العلماء في هذه المسألة، فذهب أبو الحسن الأشعري: إلى أن الوجود هو نفس الذات، وعلى هذا لا يقال إن الوجود صفة، لأن الصفة اسم للأمر الزائد على الموصوف، وعلى هذا يكون عد المتكلمين والمؤلفين المصنف والشارح الوجود من الصفات الواجبة له سبحانه مشتملا على شيء من التّسامح، وسببه: أنهم رأوا أنه يصح وصف ذات الله تعالى لفظا بما يُشتق من الوجود، فيقال: «ذات الله موجودة» فلما رأوا أنَّ الوجود يكون وصفًا في اللفظ كالصفة الحقيقية في نحو قولنا: الله تعالى عالم وقادر أطلقوا لفظ الصفة على الوجود تشبيها له بها. وقال قوم منهم الرَّازِيُّ: الوجود أمر زائد على الذات، على معنى أنه صفة ثابتة في الخارج لكنها لم تصل إلى درجة الموجودات التي تشاهد وتحسُّ، فهي واسطة بين الموجود الخارجي والمعدوم، وهذا الفريق أثبت واسطة بين الموجود والمعدوم، وسمّي هذه الواسطة عنده ثلاثة: معدوم، وموجود، وحالٌ. أما الفريق الأول فليس عنده إلا حالا، فالأقسام قسمان: الموجود والمعدوم.
The first section: The psychic attribute. [Definition of the psychic attribute: And what is meant by the psychic attribute is: a positive attribute whose description indicates the essence itself without an additional meaning, such as the substance being a substance, an essence, a thing, and an existent. It outlines three matters: the meaning of existence, the meaning of its necessity for God, and the proof for God's necessary existence. The passage ends by noting the two groups' divisions: the first group only has existent and non-existent, while the second adds a third category of 'state.'

Al-Razi's Definition of Existence
Al-Razi defines existence as a state necessary for the essence, not caused.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand al-Razi's precise definition of existence and how it distinguishes existence from other attributes.

Core Idea
Existence is an inseparable state of the essence, not caused by anything else.

This lesson introduces a key definition from Imam al-Razi, foundational in kalam. Al-Razi defines existence with careful precision, using terms like 'state', 'necessary for the essence', and 'not caused by a cause'. Understanding this definition helps clarify how theologians think about the relationship between God's essence and His existence.

Guided Path
1
Read the definition and translation
Read the Arabic definition and its English translation once to get the overall meaning.
Notice the technical terms used.
2
Understand 'necessary for the essence'
This means existence is established for the essence in a way that never separates. Grasp the inseparability.
3
Appreciate 'as long as the essence exists'
This phrase emphasizes that the essence is the locus of existence; existence is realized whenever the essence is realized.
The grammar prevents misunderstanding about the pronoun.
4
Grasp 'not caused by a cause'
This eliminates any external cause for existence itself, and also helps exclude attributes that are caused.
Note that connotational attributes are caused by meanings.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والرازي ومن ينحو نحوه يعرف الوجود بأنه: «الحال الواجب للذات ما دامت الذات غير معللة بعلة» ومعنى قولهم الواجب للذات الثابت لها ثبوتاً لا ينفك عنها و«ما» في قولهم: «ما دامت الذات» مصدرية ظرفية، أي: مدة دوام الذات و«دام» تامة، وأظهروا الفاعل في قولهم: «ما دامت الذات» دفعاً لما يتوهم عند إضماره من عود الضمير على الحال، وفائدة قولهم: «ما دامت الذات» التنبيه على أن الذات ملزومة للوجود، فمتى تحققت الذات تحقق وجودها وقولهم: «غير معللة» هو بنصب «غير» على أنه حال من «الحال» ولا يصح جعل «دام» ناقصة وجعل «غير» خبرها؛ لأن الذات لا تعلل، وقولهم: «الحال» يخرج عنه صفات المعاني والصفات السلبية، لأنها ليست بحال عندهم، وهو مجرد اصطلاح، ولا مشاحة فيه، وتخرج الصفات المعنوية إما بقولهم: «ما دامت الذات» لأن دوام الصفات المعنوية بدوام الذات مع معانيها لا بدوام الذات، وإما بقولهم: «غير معللة» بعلة ويكون قولهم: «ما دامت» ليس للاحتراز، ولكن لبيان الواقع، وخروج المعنوية ب«غير معللة» لكون المعنوية تعلل بالمعاني، ألا ترى: أن القادر معلل بقيام القدرة بالذات، والمريد معلل بقيام الإرادة وهلم جرا.
And al-Razi and those who follow his method define existence as: 'The state necessary for the essence as long as the essence exists, not caused by a cause.' And the meaning of their statement 'necessary for the essence' is [that which is] established for it with an establishment that does not separate from it. And 'ma' in their statement 'ma damat al-dhat' is a verbal noun indicating time, meaning: the duration of the essence's continuance, and 'dama' is complete. And they made the agent explicit in their statement 'ma damat al-dhat' to repel what might be imagined when it is implied of the pronoun referring back to the state. And the benefit of their statement 'ma damat al-dhat' is to alert that the essence is the locus of existence, so whenever the essence is realized, its existence is realized. And their statement 'ghayr mu'allala' has 'ghayr' in the accusative as a condition from 'al-hal', and it is not valid to make 'dama' incomplete and make 'ghayr' its predicate because the essence is not caused. And their statement 'al-hal' excludes from it the attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani) and the negative attributes (al-sifat al-salbiyya), because they are not states according to them, and it is mere terminology with no dispute. And the attributes of connotational meanings (al-sifat al-ma'nawiyya) are excluded either by their statement 'ma damat al-dhat' because the continuance of the connotational attributes is with the continuance of the essence with their meanings, not with the continuance of the essence alone, or by their statement 'ghayr mu'allala bi-illa', and their statement 'ma damat' is not for exclusion but for clarifying the reality. And the exclusion of the connotational attributes by 'ghayr mu'allala' is because the connotational attributes are caused by meanings. Do you not see that the powerful (al-qadir) is caused by the subsistence of power in the essence, and the willing (al-murid) is caused by the subsistence of will, and so forth.
Source pages p. 217

Commentary
This passage presents the definition of existence (al-wujud) according to Fakhr al-Din al-Razi and his followers. It is a definition passage. First, the definition is stated: existence is 'the state necessary for the essence as long as the essence exists, not caused by a cause.' The author then explains each component. The term 'necessary for the essence' means that existence is established for the essence in a way that never separates from it. The word 'ma' in 'ma damat al-dhat' is a verbal noun indicating time, meaning 'the duration of the essence's continuance', and the verb 'dama' is complete (i.e., not needing a predicate). They made the subject explicit to avoid the misunderstanding that the pronoun might refer back to 'the state' instead of the essence. The purpose of 'ma damat al-dhat' is to emphasize that the essence is the locus of existence: whenever the essence is realized, its existence is realized. The phrase 'ghayr mu'allala' (not caused) has 'ghayr' in the accusative as a circumstantial qualifier (hal) from 'al-hal'; it is not valid to treat 'dama' as incomplete with 'ghayr' as its predicate because the essence itself is not caused. The term 'al-hal' (the state) excludes the attributes of meanings (sifat al-ma'ani) and negative attributes (sifat salbiyya) because these are not considered 'states' in this terminology—it is merely a conventional usage with no dispute. The connotational attributes (sifat ma'nawiyya) are excluded either by 'ma damat al-dhat' because their continuance depends on the essence together with their meanings, not on the essence alone, or by 'ghayr mu'allala' because connotational attributes are caused by meanings, as exemplified by the powerful being caused by power and the willing by will.

الوجود
الحال
الواجب للذات
غير معللة
الصفات المعنوية

Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think 'ghayr mu'allala' is a predicate of 'dama', making the essence caused.
Correction: The author clarifies that 'ghayr' is in the accusative as a circumstantial qualifier from 'al-hal', and it is not valid to treat 'dama' as incomplete with 'ghayr' as its predicate because the essence itself is not caused.

Checkpoint
Why is 'ghayr' in 'ghayr mu'allala' in the accusative case?
A) Because it is the predicate of 'dama'
B) Because it is a circumstantial qualifier (hal) from 'al-hal'
C) Because it is the object of a verb
D) Because it is a definite noun

Key Takeaway
Al-Razi defines existence as a state of the essence that is inseparable and uncaused, distinguishing it from caused attributes.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
Al-Razi defines existence as inseparable from the essence and uncaused. But your existence is caused by God. Does your daily life reflect a deep awareness that you are contingent upon Him every moment, or do you act as if your existence is self-sufficient?
?
If existence is a state that is always with the essence, what does it mean for you that your own essence (your very self) is not self-subsisting? How should this truth shape your reliance on Allah, the Self-Subsisting (Al-Qayyum)?
?
The definition distinguishes existence from caused attributes. Are there areas in your life where you treat your own existence—or your abilities—as if they are uncaused, forgetting that they are gifts from Allah? How will you change that starting today?
